## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard object modeled by kinetic rate laws in chemical reaction engineering and chemical kinetics. With only (t, A) available, plausible models are autonomous or explicitly time-dependent kinetic ODEs representing reaction order, reversibility/relaxation to equilibrium, autocatalysis, inhibition, or external forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption; e.g., catalyst-saturated regime)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decomposition, radioactive-like decay of a species)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or pseudo-second-order when other reactant ~ A)
- n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (general empirical rate law / effective reaction order)
- Linear relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1; reversible-first-order net rate)
- Time-varying first-order rate coefficient: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (temperature/illumination/programmed conditions changing with time)
- Polynomial-in-time forcing: dA_dt = -A * (c0 + c1 * t + c2 * t**2) (effective k(t) approximated by a low-order series)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-like consumption/production: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating formation with depletion/carrying-capacity limit)
- Product-inhibited (rational) rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate slows as A grows due to inhibition/limited active sites; rational saturation in A)
- Mixed-order (parallel paths): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first- and second-order loss channels)
- Reversible/production plus decay: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant source/formation balanced by first-order loss; common in CSTR/transient source terms)
- Stretched-exponential time modulation: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t**c2) * A (rate coefficient that decays in time due to deactivation/aging)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Reaction order identification: dA_dt proportional to A, A**2, or A**n indicates first-, second-, or n-th order kinetics; log-log slope of |dA_dt| vs A relates to order.
- Reversibility/equilibrium: a factor (A - c) implies a stable fixed point at A = c (net rate goes to zero at equilibrium).
- Parallel pathways: sums of distinct A-dependent terms (e.g., A and A**2) suggest multiple simultaneous mechanisms with different orders.
- Autocatalysis and self-limitation: terms like A*(c - A) indicate growth at low A with slowdown near a limiting concentration (positive feedback plus depletion).
- External condition programming: explicit time dependence k(t) multiplying A (e.g., exp(c*t), polynomial in t) implies changing temperature, light, feed, or catalyst activity over time.
- Catalyst deactivation/aging: a decreasing k(t) (e.g., exp(-c*t) or exp(-c*t**n)) reflects loss of activity leading to progressively slower kinetics even at the same A.
- Inhibition/saturation in A: rational forms A/(A+c) indicate diminishing incremental rate at high A due to inhibition, site saturation, or transport limitations.
- Source terms vs pure decay: an additive constant (c0 - c1*A) indicates net production/feeding plus removal, not a closed single-species decay.
